Add built-in closet systems with adjustable shelving rods and drawers to triple your storage capacity in bedrooms. Install L-shaped corner shelves to display decorative items while providing storage in living rooms. Add corner cabinet organizers in kitchens to access hard-to-reach spaces efficiently. Create custom corner storage units with diagonal doors to maximize accessibility in bedrooms or home offices.\\n\\nSecret Storage Furniture Designs\\n\\nInvest in dual-purpose furniture pieces that conceal storage compartments. Choose ottoman coffee tables with hidden compartments for blankets and magazines. Select headboards with built-in shelving and concealed storage panels. Opt for window seats with lift-up tops to store rarely used items. Choose leather or fabric ottomans with hinged lids to store blankets magazines & seasonal items. Select models featuring removable serving trays that convert them into coffee tables. Install wall-mounted desks that fold down when needed & disappear when not in use. Choose console tables with pull-out surfaces that expand from slim hallway pieces into full dining tables seating up to six people.\\n\\nSpace-Saving Murphy Beds\\n\\nMurphy beds offer the ultimate solution for dual-purpose rooms by transforming from beds to vertical storage units. Select models with built-in shelving desks or sofas that remain accessible when the bed is folded up. Standard stud spaces measure 14-16 inches wide perfect for narrow storage solutions that don’t protrude into your living area.\\n\\nSpace-Efficient Kitchen Storage Hacks\\n\\nTransform your cramped kitchen into an organized culinary haven with these innovative storage solutions designed for maximum efficiency in minimal space.\\n\\nPull-Out Pantry Systems\\n\\nInstall slim pull-out pantry units in those narrow gaps between appliances or cabinets to create instant storage space. These vertical systems slide out smoothly to reveal multiple tiers of shelving perfect for canned goods spices and dry ingredients. Choose units with adjustable shelves and clear containers to maximize visibility and accessibility. Modern pull-out systems feature soft-close mechanisms and can hold up to 400 pounds while occupying just 6 inches of floor space.\\n\\nMagnetic Storage Solutions\\n\\nMount magnetic strips on backsplashes or the sides of cabinets to store metal utensils knives and spice containers. Create a vertical herb garden using magnetic planters or attach magnetic hooks for hanging measuring cups and cooking tools. Strong neodymium magnetic bars can support up to 40 pounds while magnetic spice tins free up valuable cabinet space. Install magnetic paper towel holders under upper cabinets to keep counters clear.\\n\\nCabinet Door Organizers\\n\\nTransform cabinet doors into valuable storage real estate with over-the-door organizers designed for pot lids cutting boards or cleaning supplies. Install adhesive hooks for measuring spoons or mount wire baskets for food wrap and aluminum foil. Clear acrylic organizers work perfectly for storing pantry items while tiered systems maximize vertical space. These organizers typically hold 3-5 pounds per hook and install without damaging cabinet doors.\\n\\nStorage Solution | Space Saved | Weight Capacity\\nPull-Out Pantry | 6″ width | 400 lbs\\nMagnetic Strips | 0″ depth | 40 lbs\\nDoor Organizers | 0″ depth | 3-5 lbs/hook\\nInnovative Bathroom Storage Solutions\\n\\nOver-the-Toilet Storage Units\\n\\nTransform wasted vertical space with over-the-toilet storage units that maximize your bathroom’s potential. Choose adjustable units with built-in towel bars or opt for floating shelves with hidden brackets that create an airy modern look. Opt for rust-resistant stainless steel or aluminum options with adjustable shelves & built-in hooks for loofahs razors & washcloths. Consider installing a second shower rod behind your shower curtain for hanging mesh organizers or adding suction-cup holders with quick-dry features for frequently used items.\\n\\nVanity Space Optimization\\n\\nMaximize your vanity’s storage potential with pull-out drawer organizers & stackable containers designed for bathroom essentials. Install sliding cabinet organizers to access items at the back of deep cabinets or add door-mounted holders for hair tools & cleaning supplies. Use magnetic strips inside cabinet doors for bobby pins & small metal items or incorporate clear acrylic organizers to separate makeup & personal care products while maintaining visibility.\\n\\nOrganizing Small Closets Like a Pro\\n\\nCloset Zone Planning\\n\\nTransform your cramped closet into a functional space by dividing it into specific zones. Create designated areas for frequently worn items at eye level hanging shoes at the bottom tier & seasonal items up high. Use drawer organizers to establish mini-zones within larger compartments such as separate sections for socks underwear & accessories. Install shelf dividers to maintain neat vertical stacks of folded items like sweaters & jeans while preventing toppling.\\n\\nSpace-Saving Hangers and Tools\\n\\nSwitch to ultra-thin velvet hangers to instantly triple your hanging space capacity. Install cascading hooks or tiered hangers to vertically stack multiple items like pants scarves or tanks. Add pull-out valet rods for outfit planning & maximize corner spaces with rotating carousel organizers. Use shower curtain rings on hangers to loop scarves belts & ties saving valuable rod space while keeping accessories visible & wrinkle-free.\\n\\nSeasonal Storage Rotation\\n\\nImplement a twice-yearly rotation system for your wardrobe based on weather patterns. Store off-season clothes in vacuum-sealed bags under the bed or on high shelves to protect them from dust & moisture. Label storage containers clearly with contents & season for easy retrieval. While the mega-mansions of the world might try to fool you into thinking small equates to bad, trust us when we say there are plenty of perks to living in a smaller space—you just have to be a bit more restrained in your decorating choices.\\nSince you don't have as much empty space to fill, you'll want to make sure every piece of decor you add to your space works with the limited layout and captures your aesthetic. Finding the right pieces to make your small kitchen or tiny powder room feel curated and not cluttered can be tricky, but it's doable. Even if you already know what you want for your space, a bit of expert inspiration can make all the difference. Designer Dane Austin chose to keep the entertaining area simple with a freestanding banquette and trio of chairs.\\nTour the Entire Space\\n\\nChristian Harder\\n2\\nUtilize Your Windows\\nIn Serena Dugan's Shelter Island, New York, vacation home, even the window frames have extra functionality. Here, a window seat gives guests a place to rest while above, low-profile bookshelves keep the floor clear of clutter. These are great tips for those short on both seating and storage.\\nTour the Entire Home\\nAdvertisement - Continue Reading Below\\n\\nBrie Williams\\n3\\nUse Multifunctional Furniture\\nIn our 2024 Whole Home's game room, the chess table conveniently folds up to free up space. Designer MA Allen wanted the room to accommodate whatever needs arose without adding multiple surfaces and furniture pieces.\\nTour the Entire Space\\n\\nAimée Mazzenga\\n4\\nChoose Benches, Not Chairs\\nA quick way to make your small home appear cleaner and larger is to opt for dining benches instead of chairs, like designer Wendy Labrum did here. The lack of seat backs allows the pieces to blend seamlessly into their surroundings rather than take up valuable visual space. Plus, you can always squeeze an extra person onto a bench.\\nTour the Entire Home\\nAdvertisement - Continue Reading Below\\n\\nNicole Franzen\\n5\\nCarve Out a Nook\\nEven the smallest of home offices can be hubs for productivity while maintaining a work/life balance. Here, designer Kelly Hurliman carved a functional workspace out of this unused alcove. Artwork and shelving make it feel intentional.\\n\\nShade Degges\\n6\\nKeep Storage Up High\\nKeeping your floors clear is an easy way to make a small entryway appear larger. In this home by designer Amber Lewis, the back entrance remains clutter-free thanks to high-hung hooks and a simple basket under the console table. The pieces keep your sightline focused on the curated decor, not how small the space is.\\nAdvertisement - Continue Reading Below\\n\\nAimee Mazzenga\\n7\\nMake Use of All Corners\\nWhen you have a small home, you need to make use of all space, including the corners. In this chic powder room by Alexandra Kaehler, the designer added a corner sink to save space, and this small home idea also adds some more visual interest to the bathroom.\\nRelated Story: Designer Alexandra Kaehler Creates an English-Inspired Interior in Chicago's North Shore\\n\\nChristian Harder\\n8\\nPut Up Open, Glass Shelves\\nOpen shelving is a great small-space solution as long as your house is not too messy or cluttered. It takes away the visual weight that closed cabinets would, and you can even take it a step further and use glass shelves, like designer Serena Dugan did here. This way, everyone gets to admire your pretty objects and you’re letting more light into every aspect of the room.\\nTour the Entire Home\\nRelated Story: Inside the “Studio Barn” Where Serena Dugan Paints—and Parties\\nAdvertisement - Continue Reading Below\\n\\nMali Azima\\n9\\nBuild Into an Existing Niche\\nSmall homes—especially old small homes—tend to have awkward little pockets of space in odd places, which means you need to tap into your creativity and figure out what that niche can be used for. In this home by Suzanne Kasler, she added a desk under this archway to give it a built-in look and take advantage of as much floor space as she could.\\nTour the Entire Home\\n\\nBrie Williams\\n10\\nFocus on Your Kitchen Storage\\nFrom pots and pans to countertop appliances, your kitchen is home to many bulky items, which is why proper storage should be high on your list of must-haves for your small home. There are plenty of small home ideas that can make your kitchen a more organized place, like peg systems in drawers or pull-out corner organizers for those deep cabinets, like what Kelsey McGregor did for our 2024 Whole Home.\\nTour the Entire Space\\nRelated Story: Inside Our Seventh Annual Whole Home\\nAdvertisement - Continue Reading Below\\n\\nErin Kelly\\n11\\nUse Appropriately Sized Furniture\\nWhen you have a small living room, don't choose the oversize sectional that'll engulf the room—shop for appropriately sized furniture that'll help the room look less cluttered. Greg Dutton from Midland Architecture and his wife, designer Liz Dutton of Liz Dutton Interiors, chose smaller, light-colored chairs and a low-to-the-ground coffee table for their living room, giving the room a more spacious feel.\\nTOUR THE ENTIRE HOME\\n\\nAlan Tansey\\n12\\nInstall a Murphy Bed\\nDon't wait for us to convince you that Murphy beds are a cool small home idea. Let this one that Michael Chen, a cofounder of architecture firm MKCA, installed in this bedroom make the case instead. This isn't just any bedroom either—it's a bedroom on a yacht where storage and floor space are in very short supply. A Murphy bed makes complete sense in this context, and the striking ribbed, powder blue frame makes it a beautiful statement.\\nRelated Story: Rollaway Beds Are the Ultimate Small-Space Hosting Hack\\nAdvertisement - Continue Reading Below\\n\\nThomas Kuoh\\n13\\nMake a Room Multipurpose\\nWhen this horizontal Murphy bed is folded up, this guest room turns back into a home office, allowing the space to exist as two things at once. Jennifer Jones of Niche Interiors really pushed the limits of this bonus room, as a hidden twin-size mattress makes so much more sense than a large sleeper sofa here.\\n\\nHagan Hinshaw\\n14\\nMake Use of Every Square Foot\\nWhen Shapeless Studio transformed this former post office into a family home, the team knew they'd need to be clever with their choices in making the structure livable. For this narrow entryway, rather than remove this hallway niche that gives the home more character, they turned it into a place to hang coats and hats. While adding an entry table or cabinet might've made the walkway more cluttered, this small home idea helps it feel larger.\\nTOUR THE ENTIRE HOME\\nRelated Story: 6 Stylish Finds to Elevate Your Entryway\\nAdvertisement - Continue Reading Below\\n\\nHagan Hinshaw\\n15\\nCustomize What You Can\\nIn the same renovation as above, the team at Shapeless Studio went with a custom table and banquette to maximize every square inch of space. Across from the bed in this attic guest bedroom is a flush door to a storage area. This clever small home idea allows extra things to remain hidden and out of the way.\\nTOUR THE ENTIRE HOME\\nAdvertisement - Continue Reading Below\\n\\nKate Starkel\\n17\\nPaint It White\\nOne of the easiest and most DIY-friendly small home ideas from designers is to simply paint it white.
